Journal on date 5/8/2002. www2.kumagaku.ac.jp Phonology and the Teaching of Kiswahili in Linguistically Diverse East African Community Jane ODUOR Introduction Kiswahili is being taught to a linguistically diverse university student population in the East African Community (EAC). A majority of these learners of Kiswahili speak a variety of other languages. Consequently, this paper aims at highlighting some aspects of Kiswahili phonetics and phonology that are either left out or not handled conclusively in Kiswahili phonology text books and the spill over into some Kiswahili phonetics and phonology classrooms, with a view to showing that there is need for a phonetic (acoustic) analysis of Standard Kiswahili sounds. The paper shows that some of the areas which are not handled adequately in Kiswahili phonetics and phonology are the Standard Kiswahili vowel chart, some vowels and consonants. This chapter identifies the possible sources of challenge to be lack of adequate research in Kiswahili phonetics and the limited number of phonology books written in Kiswahili. It is suggested that the phonetic analysis of Kiswahili using modern computer software programs such as Praat and Speech Analyser should be carried out. This should then contribute towards an in-depth analysis of Kiswahili phonetics and phonology and the writing of text books on the same subject. The paper then concludes that this kind of analysis will lift up Kiswahili in terms of research, innovation and teaching to the level of analysis attained for the other big languages of the world. The main inspiration for this chapter arises from interactions with Kiswahili text books written for secondary school students, university level Standard Kiswahili text books on phonology, Kamusi ya Kiswahili Sanifu and conversations with some of the phonetics and phonology lecturers at the University of Nairobi. For meaningful oral communication, correct pronunciation is paramount. Teaching the phonology of a language reinforces the ability of students to articulate correctly. Therefore, Kiswahili phonology text books need to be appropriate to meet expectations of Standard Kiswahili. The paper begins by establishing a relationship between phonetics and phonology and the teaching of Kiswahili, and then goes on to explain how data for this research was obtained. It then identifies and shows the areas found to create a challenge in or to be inadequate in the teaching of Standard Kiswahili phonetics and phonology and their possible solutions or remedies. It also discusses other challenges that could be the source of the inadequacies. The paper ends with conclusion and recommendations. Linguistics and the Teaching of Kiswahili at University The relationship between linguistics and language teaching has always been a controversial one with many linguists arguing that linguistics has nothing to say to the teacher (see Sampson, 1980). On the other hand, Johnson (1982) says that language teachers have always looked to the linguist for guidance on how to teach languages. To Johnson, linguistics is considered as something of a mother discipline to the teaching of language. Both the language teacher and the linguist are concerned with language: the former with what the latter studies and describes (Halliday, McIntosh and Strevens 1964). Therefore, phonology is a field of study relevant to teaching Kiswahili. The aim of this chapter is to assess the teaching of Kiswahili at university level in a linguistically diverse context that is the EAC. This evaluation is significant as it illustrates how phonology is essential for the teaching of Kiswahili at university. It is important to do this because the relationship between phonology and language teaching is an indirect one and teachers expect linguistics to say something to them. Chomskian analysis of language has made teachers expect alternative answers to linguistic questions that can guide their teaching. Linguistics is looked upon by teachers to provide new ideas into language teaching. Chomsky's view of language as a system of rules implies that perception and awareness of rules precedes the use of these rules, and that a conscious grammatical understanding of a language rule should precede the provision of opportunities for practice in language teaching (Chastain, 1971). To Chomsky, the creative characteristics of language should lead to the rejection of mechanical practice and instead emphasise on the creative an innovative use of the language. Proponents of this line of thinking seek to allow a learner to depend on their innate capacity and to control the learning process themselves (see Newmark, 1966; Newmark and Reibel, 1968). Developments in linguistic theory since the 1970s have witnessed a shift away from the study of language seen purely as a formal system towards the study of language as communication. This trend accounts for a shift towards sociolinguistics, discourse analysis, semantics, speech act theory and pragmatics as fields of study in linguistics. All these theories have impacted in a major way on language teaching. The culmination of linguistic models and views in a communicative approach to language study has to be understood, in part as a reaction against the predominant formalistic view of language teaching. Effective communication depends on the immediate and automatic access to linguistic forms so that the mind can consciously engage in the more creative business of negotiating meaning. If these forms were not internalized as habitual mental patterns independent of thought, they could not be readily accessed and language could not function effectively as a means of thinking and communicating (Widdowson (1990: ll). A major impact of linguistic concepts, notions and functions has been in syllabus design which specifies learners' roles, settings and topics, and language activities (Wilkins, 1976; Van Ek, 1975). Krashen’s (1982) research illustrates the increasing influence of linguistics on the challenges of teaching and learning of a language. Linguistics should only be applied and used in language teaching within pedagogical principles and not in abstractness and intricacy. Fragmentary and incomplete application of linguistics to language teaching can easily fail to achieve the intended objectives owing to the development of nonfunctional syllabuses. Language teaching is dynamic and not static (Widdowson,1979, 1990; Gregg, 1984; Lennon, 1989). Pedagogical Principles of Teaching Kiswahili at Universities in the EAC The process of EAC integration, coupled with internationalization and globalization of higher education in the region and beyond, has led to increased student mobility across Partner States. With Article 137 of the EAC Treaty providing for Kiswahili to be the Language of Wider Communication, and following East African Legislative Assembly (EALA) Resolution of 2016 to make Kiswahili an Official Language of the Community, Kiswahili is becoming important and more widespread. More and more universities are establishing Kiswahili courses which itself reflects a growing demand for the language. Teaching and learning of a language is concerned with micro- and macro-skills. According to Klimova (2014), there are eight pedagogical principles to be considered in the teaching of any language for various purposes. These are: Promoting constructivism and connectivism as background philosophies; Exploiting corpus linguistics as a resource for the teaching of specific genres; Using task-based activities; iv. Exploiting authentic materials and tasks; Promoting learner autonomy; Using blended learning; Integrating cooperative and collaborative learning; and Employing team teaching. Constructivism and connectivism are the two most utilized perspectives and representations of concepts and content in which languages are presented and encouraged. Kiswahili language education curriculum should be designed to incorporate activities, opportunities, tools and environments that encourage self-regulation, self-analysis, self-reflection and self-awareness. In teaching language, learning situations, environments, skills, content and tasks ought to be relevant, realistic, authentic and that seek to replicate the natural complexities of the real world of learners. Learners should be enabled to construct knowledge independently and not just reproduce it. This knowledge construction should take place in individual contexts through negotiation, collaboration and experience in problem-solving, higher-order thinking skills and deep understanding. Connor (2013) and Flowerdew (2012) recommend that language teaching should take place by means of authentic, naturally occurring data produced by a variety of users. This moves the study of language away from ideas of what is correct, towards what is typical or frequent (Sinclair, 1991). The teaching of Kiswahili should describe features that define the language. Learners of Kiswahili can increase their linguistic proficiency by looking at grammatical and lexical issues in the language. This use of corpus linguistics, as Barlow (2002) argues, can be applied in teaching language, including Kiswahili, in three main areas: syllabus design that meets leaner needs; Materials development that provide learner discovery; and classroom activities that promote learner discovery and autonomy. In a Task-Based Language Learning approach, learners are made to work cooperatively in groups in solving different tasks (Willis & Willis 2007). This encourages learners to develop a deeper understanding of a language through the development of metacognitive skills of critical thinking and reflection (Vermillion 1997). This model provides insights in teaching Kiswahili at universities in the EAC by having courses that allow teachers act as coordinators and facilitators and by participating in activities whose content is provided by students through group interaction and whose outcomes are not determined beforehand. Language education ought to prioritize authentic texts and other teaching materials (Dudley-Evans & St John 1998; Plews 2010; Todd, 2003) even though non-authentic materials better serve pedagogical purposes (Ellis, 2003). Kiswahili students can benefit from authentic texts which should be attractive and link learners’ world to the outside world. Kiswahili reading materials should expose learners to current topics from various language domains. Autonomous learning expects learners to be mature, self-directed and motivated (Todd, 2003; Waters & Waters 1992, 1995) and involves learners being aware of their own ways of learning, so as to utilize their strengths and work on their weaknesses (van Lier 1996). Kiswahili learners should be ready to realize themselves and needs, and be determined to take on responsibilities, seek knowledge and information independently, and be willing to cooperate and communicate with others and show empathy to other people. Technologies help learners and teachers to work together to improve the quality of blended learning and teaching, with the aim of providing realistic practical opportunities to make learning independent, useful, sustainable and ever growing (Bruffee, 1993; Graham, et al, 2003; 2005). Hence, blended learning should be employed in the teaching of Kiswahili as it is likely to support more interactive strategies than only face-to-face teaching. Kiswahili education at university will also encourage collaborative learning with students and educators working together on academic projects from anywhere and at any time. Blended learning of Kiswahili will help reduce costs of implementation of the curriculum. But even as blended learning of Kiswahili is being considered, it has to be remembered that it is time-consuming and costly in terms of creating materials and preparation and evaluation. The approach assumes readiness of students’ study skills. Another approach would be integration of collaborative and cooperative learning that involves smallgroup active student participation. The former approach can take place any time and allows students to work together towards a goal while in the latter students work together in the same place on a given task. Kiswahili students can raise their inter-cultural awareness while working together as a team and each member contributing to reach a compromise in raising their proficiency. The last approach necessary for consideration is teamteaching at two major levels: cooperation in course design and implementation; and, collaboration between teachers and students to develop course outlines and the curriculum (Dudley-Evans, 2001; Flowerdew & Peacock, 2001). Kiswahili can be taught with two or more specialists working together in order to improve their students’ skills. The foregoing methodological principles and approaches are not mutually exclusive. Instead, they should be seen as complementing each other in promoting the teaching of Kiswahili at university level in the EAC. Some Areas of concern and possible remedies in the Teaching of Kiswahili Phonology Based on library research on information in Kiswahili phonology books written mostly by researchers in Kenya and Tanzania, and an examination of some segmental aspects as discussed in the text books reveals that there are areas that seem to have a challenge. Further, interviews conducted with phonology lecturers and students taking Kiswahili phonetics and phonology at the University of Nairobi showed areas of concern or challenges. Possible remedies to these concerns are discussed in this chapter. Kiswahili Vowels An analysis of some Kiswahili phonemes in the vowel chart yields interesting findings about the vowel [a]. Though the main interest in this section is in the presentation of information in university level text books, secondary school level text books are mentioned where necessary because the writers of some of these books are university professors, some of whom teach Kiswahili phonetics and phonology. The inadequacies in the presentation of information concerning Kiswahili pronunciation found in secondary school books have been addressed by researchers such as Oduor (2012). It was found that there are varying charts used for teaching Standard Kiswahili vowels. Since it is assumed that there is only one Standard Kiswahili, one would expect that the chart should also be standard. The variations give the impression that there is no Standard Kiswahili. While there are varieties of Kiswahili, a phonetic investigation of the different sounds has not been carried out. Two of the charts that are found in Kiswahili text books used for teaching are presented below: Figure 1: Taken from Habwe and Matei (2006) Figure 2: Taken from Massamba et al. (2004, pg. 25) The two vowel charts above look quite different from one another. The two charts presented in Iribe Mwangi (2008) are different from the ones presented in Figures (1) and (2). This already gives a total of four different charts for Standard Kiswahili. Whereas Figure (1) shows that /a/ is more central than back, in Figure (2) /a/ it is a bit more to the back. These variations are also discussed in Oduor (2012) for secondary school books. For this sound an acoustic analysis is required to find out if there are any variations and where the variations occur. This will show if the sound /a/ is more back than central, hence it will be clear if Kiswahili has either the sound /a/ or /a/. Whereas the former symbol represents a more central or front low vowel, the latter represents a low back vowel. The reason for the disparities in the positions of the vowels themselves and the shapes of the vowel charts is lack of scientific research and testing of Kiswahili vowels in the current literature. Closely related to the issues discussed in the preceding paragraph is the identification of long vowels such as /a:/ as opposed to a sequence of similar vowels separated by syllable boundary. The word ‘maana’ /ma-a-na/, which means ‘meaning’, is an example of the latter. The symbol ‘-’ in the word represents syllable boundary. The word ‘saa’ /sa:/, which means ‘time’, is an example of the former. The area of vowel length is another area that needs an acoustic analysis. Generally, an acoustic study of Kiswahili vowels is necessary so that their positions of articulation are identified. This will also lead to the development of one standard chart for Standard Kiswahili vowels in the whole of the East African region and the world at large. The data used for this kind of investigation should contain Standard Kiswahili vowels in different positions within words. The same vowel should occur with different Kiswahili phonemes so that the full range of pronunciation of these vowels may be captured or identified. At the same time if this is done as recommended any allophonic variations that are there in the Kiswahili vowels will emerge naturally and be identified. This kind of study is important because it will give a reliable distribution of Kiswahili vowels. A study of vowel length dichotomy can also be carried out effectively using Praat or Speech Analyser. To discuss Kiswahili vowels more conclusively, there is need to discuss the features [ATR] and [tense] for Kiswahili vowels more thoroughly. Kiswahili is a Bantu language. Most Bantu languages in Kenya have [+ATR] (Advanced Tongue Root) and [-ATR] (Retracted Tongue Root) dichotomy which seems to be different from the notion of [+tense] and [-tense], respectively. There is need to investigate the motivation for characterizing Kiswahili vowels in terms of the feature [tense] and not [ATR]. According to Ladefoged and Johnson (2011) [+ATR] and [-ATR] vowels: … differ primarily in the size of the pharynx. In the one set, there are vowels in which the root of the tongue is drawn forward and the larynx is lowered, so that the part of the vocal tract in the pharynx is considerably enlarged. These vowels are called advanced tongue root (or, more simply, +ATR) vowels. In the other set, there are vowels in which there is no advancement of the tongue root or lowering of the larynx (-ATR vowels). (pp. 228-229) The [+ATR] vowels have a tendency to be higher than their [-ATR] counterparts. According to Odden (2005), the difference between [i] and [] is one of vowel height. He goes on to state that this vowel contrast is described in terms of [ATR] for African and Siberian languages. He then introduces the debate about the phonetic difference between [ATR] and [tense] by stating that: Typically, [+tense] front vowels are fronter than their lax counterparts, and [+tense] back vowels are backer than their lax counterparts. In comparison, [+ATR] vowels are supposed to be generally fronter than corresponding [-ATR] vowels …. However, some articulatory studies have shown that the physical basis for the tense/lax distinction in English is no different from that which ATR is based on. Unfortunately, the clearest examples of the feature [ATR] are found in languages of Africa, where very little phonetic research has been done. (p. 141) It is possible to carry out this kind of phonetic study for Standard Kiswahili vowels. There is clearly a research gap that should be filled in not only for the vowels of Kiswahili but also for the numerous vowels of the numerous African languages. Odden (2005) goes on to say that no language contrasts both [ATR] and [tense] vowels. So the question is: are there phonetic studies which show clearly that for Kiswahili it is [tense] and not [ATR] that exists and not vice versa? As far as the investigation I have carried out is concerned, there seems to be no current acoustic study that has established whether it is the feature [tense] or [ATR] that exists in Standard Kiswahili. Kiswahili Consonants Apart from vowels, some consonants do not also have a conclusive analysis. One consonant whose phonemic status is questionable or should be investigated further is [], the labiodental nasal. In Iribe-Mwangi (2010), it appears in the consonant chart within slanted slashes. This seems to suggest that it is regarded as a consonant phoneme in Standard Kiswahili by this researcher yet it is impossible to use the minimal pair test to prove that it is one. Its occurrence is restricted as it only occurs before /v/. So, it must be a variant of another sound. It occurs in words such as follows: Mvivu [vivu] ‘lazy (adjective in reference to person)’ Mvua [vua] ‘rain’ Mvulana [vulana] ‘boy’ The nasal sounds that have been established to exist in Kiswahili as phonemes are /m, n, , /. It is my observation that some students have been led to believe that in the articulation of nasals, air passes through the nasal as well as the oral cavity. This analysis comes about as a result of attaching a vowel sound to the production of the nasal consonant. For example, in producing the sound /m/ in a classroom situation, a teacher may produce the sound as [ma] thus adding a vowel to this articulation to make it audible to all students. When that is done, air is allowed to pass out into the atmosphere through the mouth during the vowel articulation. To avoid this error in teaching, it would be easier to expose learners to the articulation of these nasals in words where they are used as syllabic consonant. A few examples of Kiswahili words with nasal sounds are given in (2) to show the environment where they function as syllabic consonants. Mtoto [-to-to] ‘child’ Mtu [m-tu] ‘person’ Mbunge [m-bu-] ‘Member of Parliament’ Nje [-] ‘outside’ Nzi [n-zi] ‘house fly’ Since in pronouncing the words in (2), one must complete the first syllable before moving to the next, it would be clear that in the production of nasals air passes out into the atmosphere through the nose. An acoustic analysis of nasals in Kiswahili would help to address this challenge. The emerging spectrograms in an acoustic analysis of Kiswahili sounds using Praat or Speech Analyser would show the acoustic characteristics of nasal sounds as opposed to the oral ones. In acoustic terms, the production of nasals in Kiswahili may not be different from that of the other well studied languages like English. Some researchers at the University of Nairobi have observed that some Standard Kiswahili speakers use //, the voiced palato-alveolar affricate, instead of the palatal stop / / which exists in Standard Kiswahili. Some of the words which contain this sound are listed in (3) below. Jenga [-a] ‘build’ Jela [-la] ‘prison’ Taja [ta-a] ‘mention’ Uji [u-i] ‘porrodge’ The impression given is that the words in (3) are pronounced with the sound // as seen in (4). Jenga [-a] ‘build’ Jela [-la] ‘prison’ Taja [ta-a] ‘mention’ Uji [u-i] ‘porridge’ There are Kenyan languages such as Dholuo where palato-alveolar affricates [] and [] are seen to occur in free variation with palatal stops [] and [], respectively. There are many Kenyan languages with this sound. So, this could be a case of transfer from mother tongue to Kiswahili. Many languages in the East African region also have it. Once again, an acoustic analysis of audio recordings of Standard Kiswahili speakers would clearly show which sound exists in Standard Kiswahili. Hence it would be more clearer if the use of [] is simply a case of mother tongue interference. Iribe-Mwangi (2008) presents /x/, the voiceless velar fricative, in the consonant chart whereas Mwaliwa (2014) does not. Though this may not require an acoustic investigation, more investigation needs to be carried out by researchers in phonology to establish its status in Standard Kiswahili. Another controversial area would be the analysis of prenasalised consonants or nasal compounds as referred to in some researches. Some researchers view them as consonant clusters as seen in the analysis given to them in syllables. When they occur in syllables, they are analyzed as CC sequences which gives the impression that they are a cluster and not one C that is internally complex. Iribemwangi (2010) and Mwaliwa (2014) represent them as CC sequences. A cluster then implies that the articulation of one sound is completed or almost completed before the onset of the next sound. In my view they are single internally complex segments that should be analysed as unit phonemes. They are internally complex, just as the affricates [] and [], which have two phases of articulation. For affricates, the first phase is a stop phase followed by a second one which is a fricative phase. For prenasalised consonants, the first phase is a nasal stop phase while the second one is an oral stop one. Since this kind of research and analysis is not yet visible in Kiswahili phonology text books, there is need for an acoustic analysis of this set of sounds. Some prenasalised consonants occur in words such the ones listed in (5) below. Their varied analysis in terms of Cs and Vs is also displayed. Existing Analysis Proposed Analysis Mboga [-] [CCV-CV] or [CV-CV] ‘vegetable’ Kitanda [--] [CV-CV-CCV] or [CV-CV-CV] ‘bed’ Gonga [-] [CV-CCV] or [CV-CV] ‘hit’ Vunja [-] [CV-CCV] or [CV-CV] ‘break’ This then is another area that calls for an acoustic analysis using audio recordings from competent speakers of Standard Kiswahili so that Kiswahili phonetics and phonology are taught competently within the East African region. An acoustic analysis would show if, for Kiswahili, it is the existing analysis or the proposed one in (5) that is correct. A proper research must stem from this region because East Africa is the home of Kiswahili and this is where its mother tongue speakers are found. As observed in the discussions in this section, all the issues discussed involve sound segments. When sound segments are studied well or conclusively, it becomes easy to deal with the other phonological levels. It is therefore recommended in this study that the main and possibly the only remedy to these varied and controversial analysis is an acoustic analysis of all the sound segments that exist in Standard Kiswahili. The question of whether they exist as phonemes or allophones should come after the phonetic analysis. Sources of Challenges of Teaching Kiswahili Phonology There are challenges that may have led to the inadequacies discussed in the preceding sections. The first one is that the books lecturers use to teach Kiswahili phonetics and phonology are the same ones used for teaching general phonetics and phonology. Some of these text books are Abercrombie (1967), O’connor (1973) and Ladefoged (1995). To an extent this is correct if they are teaching general phonetics and phonology to Kiswahili students to give them a proper foundation or a wider view of the sounds that exist in human language. Books that focus on Kiswahili phonetics specifically are required. Lack of general phonetics and phonology books, such as Clark and Yallop (1995) and Abercrombie (1967) written in Kiswahili is yet another challenge. To enable students and other researchers to be competent in the terminology used in phonetics and phonology, books need to be translated into Kiswahili with the permission of the original authors. Kiswahili researchers who are interested in its sound system should write general phonology and phonetics books in Kiswahili. A good example of such a phonology text is Massamba (2011). There are no adequate books that are based on Kiswahili phonetics to improve the teaching of Kiswahili phonology. Another challenge is that books published on Kiswahili phonology are few. Therefore, for the sound system of Kiswahili, more books that focus on Kiswahili phonology are required. There are a few researchers who have already written such books on Kiswahili phonology. A good example is Massamba et al. (2004). It was observed that sometimes the texts used were written several years ago, for example, Polome (1967). The content may still be relevant but there may be sections that need to be updated to be in line with the modern trends. Researchers may need to volunteer to update such books and improve on section that may not be good enough in terms of detailed research. An example of a book of phonetics that was updated is Ladefoged (1975). It is now Ladefoged and Johnson (2014). The sixth edition of this same text was published in 2011. Hence it is updated frequently. It is noted that Habwe & Karanja (2004) was also updated and reprinted after this first publication. Yet another challenge is related to the time provided for teaching Kiswahili to students. This is especially a major problem in the Bachelor of Education programme where students have to take Kiswahili (both language and literature) as one teaching subject in addition to another teaching subject unlike their counterparts in the same programme who take English language and literature as two teaching subjects. The same problem exists in the Bachelor of Arts programme where students who want to major in Kiswahili have to learn Kiswahili linguistics and literature (isimu na fasihi), unlike their counterparts who can choose to major in linguistics only or literature. Students of Kiswahili especially in the Bachelor of Arts programme should be allowed to major in either Linguistics or Literature so that they have ample time to delve deep into the subject. Kiswahili University Textbooks and the Teaching of Phonology and Phonetics This discusses the relationship between phonetics and phonology for it is in this relationship that the ultimate solution lies. According to Clark and Yallop (1995), both phonetics and phonology are concerned with speech, that is, the way speech is heard and produced. Phonetics focuses more narrowly on articulation and acoustics, while phonology deals with the systematic organization and structures of speech sounds. According to Laver (2000), phonology is intimately connected with the phonetic study of speech. Whereas Clark and Yallop (1995) state that the boundary between phonetics and phonology should not be drawn sharply, Laver (2000) states that neither of them is feasible without an adequate understanding of the other. This close relationship is also discussed by Massamba (2010). He notes that they are closely related disciplines and cites Trubetzkoy (1969) in stating that: ‘As regards phonology, it is clear that it make[s] use of certain phonetic concepts’ (p. 14). He further states that “… although we have said that phonetics deals with speech sounds in general, it should be noted that it is possible to simply study the phonetics of a particular language without having recourse to ‘universal phonetics’.” Therefore, a proper study of Kiswahili phonology includes a proper understanding of Kiswahili phonetics. Hence, this paper has attempted to show that there is need to work more on Kiswahili phonetics especially at the level of its acoustics in order to understand Kiswahili phonology more and teach it more competently. We, as researchers of Kiswahili phonology and phonetics, need to do more research in order to clarify issues that still remain hazy or unclear. If we look at languages such as English, German, French, etc, there are many books that are specific to their phonetics and phonology. Such books help to reduce ambiguities in phonological analysis. For English two examples of such text are Jones (1972) and Roach (2009). Sound phonological theories are also developed from and supported by phonological and phonetic language data that is convincing. Researchers of Kiswahili in the East African Countries should be willing to take time to carry out thorough investigations. They must take the lead in generating knowledge of Kiswahili. They should also take the lead in disseminating the knowledge gathered from research. There seems to be no standard chart for teaching Kiswahili vowels. Secondly, the phonemic status of the consonant [] is questionable. Thirdly, some students have been led to believe that in the articulation of nasals, air passes through both the nasal and the oral cavities. Fourthly, some researchers have observed that some Standard Kiswahili speakers use // instead of / / in Standard Kiswahili. Lastly, the prenasalized consonants are viewed by some researchers as unit phonemes while others seem to view them as consonant clusters. The sources of the challenge in teaching Kiswahili phonology are twofold. Firstly, the books lecturers use to teach Kiswahili phonology and phonetics are the same ones used for teaching general phonetics and phonology. There are no adequate books that are based on Kiswahili phonetics to improve the teaching of Kiswahili phonology. Secondly, sometimes the texts used were written several years ago. Thirdly, there is inadequate time provided for teaching Kiswahili linguistic to students. It is recommended that a proper study of Kiswahili phonology includes a proper understanding of Kiswahili phonetics and that general phonology and phonetics books should be written in Kiswahili. Old books which are still useful should be updated frequently. Hence, this chapter has attempted to show that we need to work more on Kiswahili phonetics especially at the level of its acoustics using computer software such as Praat and Speech Analyser in order to understand Kiswahili phonology better and teach it more competently. There is need to carry out a thorough phonetic analysis of Kiswahili and write books both in Kiswahili phonetics and phonology so that researchers and teachers of Kiswahili can have a proper beginning point. The Need for Kiswahili Phonology Curriculum Review at University Level in the EAC From the discussion above, there is need for curriculum review and redevelopment of Kiswahili Phonology as taught in universities in the EAC. The aim is to enhance student learning, engagement, experience and outcomes. The process of review and enhancement of Kiswahili Phonology curriculum can be a valuable developmental process for both individuals and programme teams involved in the teaching and learning of this course. If planned and executed well, review has the potential to improve Kiswahili phonology teaching and learning, leading to a stronger programme tin Kiswahili education at university level. Departments of Kiswaili should have curriculum review embedded into their culture. They should have a curriculum framework review to embark on a more ambitious curriculum change programme of particularly Phonetics and Phonology courses but generally all Kiswahili courses. This reform is necessary in response to the changing nature of linguistics and opportunities offered by new learning technologies. Academic leadership is required to initiate and sustain the envisaged curriculum review and reform. Necessary measures are necessary for proper planning, communicating, sustaining and evaluating the impact of curriculum review and any subsequent enhancements on the Kiswahili Phonology curriculum. Hence, there is need for a coherent, coordinated and structured approach to Kiswahili programme design which is necessary for effective curriculum change. A collaborative environment is desirable where staff are given the opportunity to shape the curriculum that ultimately they will be required to implement with students having a strong stake as partners in shaping curriculum and assessment design. Universities in the EAC need to make it a point to be reviewing their Kiswahili programmes over a specific period of time. Periodic reviews and accreditation will inform the development of undergraduate and postgraduate Kiswahili programmes in new areas of study. Staff development and training needs have to be identified and built into the plan for the review of Kiswahili curriculum at university level. This is necessary so as to develop the confidence, skills and attributes of those to be involved. The global higher education landscape is changing rapidly, and the number, scope and pace of change initiatives at University level will impact on the capacity for change in the EAC. Conclusion and Recommendations This chapter explored Kiswahili phonology course implementation issues and the place and role of university textbooks and lecturers. It has been pointed out that Kiswahili Phonetics and Phonology are key foundational courses in Kiswahili studies. These aspects of Kiswahili linguistics are not being handled satisfactorily as a result of many factors, including teachers and textbooks. Kiswahili curriculum at university level in the EAC needs a comprehensive review and reform that will lead to changes. Throughout the EAC, there is belief and faith among an increasing number of university students in the transformative power of Kiswahili. The language is seen not just as a useful skill, but as a symbol of a better life, a pathway to regional integration and sustainable development. These expectations and aspirations place a heavy burden for Kiswahili education, and for those who have responsibility for teaching it. The challenges of providing relevant Kiswahili courses and materials are significant. Nonetheless, that notwithstanding, Kiswahili is becoming a powerful agent for regional integration and sustainable development and universities in the EAC must provide requisite education. Changamoto za Ufundishaji Ngeli za Kiswahili Sanifu na Athari zake Kimatumizi John Hamu HABWE Utangulizi Ufundishaji wa Ngeli za Kiswahili Sanifu ni kipengele muhimu katika mitaala ya Kiswahili ya Vyuo Vikuu kwa kuwa humwekea mwanafunzi msingi mzuri wa kujifunza. Hata hivyo, ufundishaji wa ngeli umekumbwa na changamoto kadhaa ambazo huathiri matumizi ya Kiswahili. Hali hii husababishwa na kuwako mitazamo tofauti kuhusu kipashio hiki cha sarufi ya lugha. Pana haja ya kufundisha kwa uwazi ngeli za Kiswahili sanifu. Hivyo basi, makala hii inachunguza suala la ufundishaji na uendelezaji wa Kiswahili katika ukanda wa Afrika Mashariki. Tunajikita kwenye suala la ngeli na tumeonyesha kwamba kuna nomino hasa nomino za mkopo ambazo huzingatia mifumo miwili au hata zaidi ya ngeli kimatumizi lakini walimu wa Kiswahili nchini Kenya hufundisha nomino hizo kwa kuzingatia mfumo mmoja pekee. Hilo ni jambo ambalo linaleta mgongano baina ya ufundishaji wa nomino na matumizi yake. Data ya kazi hii ilikusanywa kutoka kwa walimu wanaofundisha katika shule za upili nchini Kenya pamoja na kutazama matumizi ya nomino husika katika vyombo vya habari na vile vile kusoma vitabu vya fasihi ili kubainisha matumizi haya. Makala hii inahoji kwamba walimu na wataalamu wengi wa Kiswahili katika vyuo vikuu na ambao walilishughulikia suala la ngeli hapo nyuma wamelifumbia jicho suala hili la uainishaji nomino kuwili na hivyo kusababisha mvutano katika uanishaji wa nomino husika. Makala hii inadai kuwa kutozingatia uainishaji kuwili shuleni kunainyima lugha ya Kiswahili nafasi ya kukua na kuwa na mifumo mbadala na kuwa na utajiri katika sarufi yake licha ya kutatiza matumizi ya nomino za aina hii katika mitagusano ya kimaendeleo katika maeneo kama vile elimu, biashara, utafiti, afya, michezo, nk katika eneo la Afrika Mashariki. Nadharia za Sarufi na Ufundishaji wa Kiswahili Suala la ufundishaji sarufi limekuwa likijadiliwa katika ufundishaji na ujifunzaji lugha kwa muda mrefu sasa (Hossein Nassaji & Sandra Fotos, 2011). Mgogoro umehusu ikiwa sarufi ifundishwa kama somo maalumu au iwe tu ni sehemu ya matukio ya elimu ya lugha inayotokea darasani. Kwa mujibu wa Kelly (1969), hali hii imekuwako tangu lugha ya mwanadamu ianze kufundishwa. Umuhimu wa mgogoro huu ni kwamba unaonyesha mitazamo tofauti iliyoko miongoni mwa walimu wa lugha na wanaisimu kuhusiana na muundo wa lugha na jinsi ya kuifunza. Hata hivyo, kuendelea kwa hali hii kunasababisha sarufi kuzidi kuwa tata katika taaluma ya elimu ya lugha na hata wakati mwingine kutosisitizwa kabisa (Stern, 1992). Utafiti wa karibuni umeonyesha haja ya kufundisha sarufi na vipengele vyake muhimu (Williams, 2005). Sarufi ndio msingi wa kuijua na kuitumia lugha. Kutoijua lugha kuna maana kwamba haiwezi kutumiwa katika ufundishaji na ujifunzaji. Kwa mujibu wa Williams, kuna nadharia nne muhimu sana katika ufundishaji wa sarufi: sarufi elekezi; sarufi elezi; sarufi muundo; na sarufi matumizi. Rothman (2010) anaifafanua sarufi elekezi kuwa mfumo wa kanuni zilizoundwa kwa msingi dhahania wa lugha. Mtazamo huu huichukulia lugha kuwa yenye mfumo kutegemea hadhi yake. Kwa mfano, sarufi elekezi inatarajia matumizi sahihi ya Kiswahili sanifu. Hivyo, kuna ‘usahihi’ na kuna ‘usanifu’ kama mambo ya kimsingi yanayotarajiwa katika matumizi ya lugha. Kwa mantiki hii, kuna muktdaha na uwanja wa matumizi. Vilevile kuna mamlaka inayokadiria na kuamua kama lugha ni sahihi na ni sanifu. Inatarajiwa kwamba kanuni za kutumia Kiswahili sahihi na sanifu zitafundishwa katika elimu kwa kuzingatia mongozo kama vile mitaala ya Kiswahili. Hivyo, nadharia hii inamwelekeza mwalimu na mwanafunzi kufuata sharia na miundo ya lugha na matumzi yake. Hata ingawa nadharia hii ni ya kale, bado ina umuhimu mkubwa katika elimu ya Kiswahili. Kwa upande mwingine, nadharia ya Sarufi elezi inaonyesha matumizi ya kila siku ya lugha katika jamii (Rothman, 2010). Nadharia hii, tofauti na Nadharia Elekezi, haimwonyeshi kanuni na kumtaka mtumiaji wa lugha kuzifuata. Badala yake, nadharia hii hupambanua jinsi ambavyo lugha hutumiwa kwa kuzingatia sarufi. Nadharia hii huonyesha ufahamu wa wazawa na watumiaji wa lugha. Mwalimu wa sarufi ya Kiswahili anaweza kuwajulisha wanafunzi kuwa lugha hii inaweza kutumiwa vizuri na kueleweka na mtu ambaye hajawahi kwenda shuleni. Usahihi na usanifu wa lugha umo katika lugha na matumizi yake. Sarufi Miundo iliibuka kutokana na nadharia za Chomsky katikati ya karne ya ishirini. Sarufi miundo inaichukulia lugha kuwa sehemu ya maumbile ya fikra za mwanadamu (William, 2005). Kufuatia mitazamo ya Chomsky, lugha inahusiana na akili za mwanadamu. Hivyo, mwanadamu ana uwezo wa kuitumia lugha kutokana na maumbile yake. Lakini pia lugha inaweza kutumiwa vizuri na mtu asiye mzawa wake. Matumizi ya lugha hayafai kufungwa na mikatale ya kanuni. Hii ni kwa sababu, lugha inaweza kuwa sahihi kimuundo lakini isiwe sahihi kimaana. Hivyo basi, usahihi wa lugha siyo kigezo cha kukadiria usanifu wake. Chomsky alishikilia kwamba watumiaji wajikite kwa ufahamu wa lugha na siyo kwa sheria walizojifunza. Msimamo wa Chomsky ni muhimu kwa mwalimu wa Kiswahili na kwa wanafunzi walioko kwenye mazingira tofauti ya kujifunza. Sarufi ma/tumizi iliasisiwa na Simon C. Dik aliyeiona lugha kuwa mpangilio wa ngazi mbalimbali zenye majukumu maalum (Williams, 2005). Sarufi hii inatokana na uchunguzi wa lugha mbalimbali. Sarufi matumizi hivyo basi inaweza kutumika kujifunza na kulinganisha lugha mbalimbali hasa kwenye ngazi za diskosi na prakmatiki. Sarufi inachukuliwa kuwa uteuzi anaofanya mtumiaji wa lugha kuchagua na kutumia vipashio mbalimbali kuunda matini yenye maana kimuktadha. Walimu wa Kiswahili wanaweza kutumia sarufi hii kufundisha lugha hii na matumizi yake katika miktadha mbalimbali. Ikumbukwe kwamba nadharia na aina za sarufi zote zina lengo la kueleza dhima ya lugha ya kimawasiliano. Mawasiliano hujengwa kutokana na matumizi na maana ya lugha kwenye muktadha. Lugha ni chombo cha mawasiliano. Lugha huitumikia jamii. Matumizi hayo yanaweza kuwa ya kawaida ya kila siku au yakawa siyo ya kawaida kama vile kwenye fasihi. Muundo, maana, matumizi, muktadha na mawasiliano hujitokeza kuwa masuala muhimu katika elimu ya lugha. Mitaala ya Kiswahili katika vyuo vikuu vya Afrika Mashariki inastahili kuonyesha hali na ngazi hizi. Mitaala ya Kiswahili ionyeshe namna Kiswahili kimeundwa; namna Kiswahili hutoa maana; namna Kiswahili hutumiwa ; namna Kiswahili hujitokeza na kueleweka kimuktadha; na namna Kiswahili huwasiliana. Ufundishaji wa Ngeli za Kiswahili Suala la ngeli katika lugha ya Kiswahili limejadiliwa kwa kina na kwa muda mrefu na wataalamu tofauti tofauti wa Kiswahili wakiwemo Zawawi (1974), Polome (1967) Myachina (1981), Kapinga (1983), Mgullu (1999), Habwe na Karanja (2004), na Mohamed (2000). Mjadala mkubwa; kama anavyodai Mukuria (2002) ni kuwa, wataalamu hawa wametaka kubaini, nomino za Kiswahili zinaweza kuainishwa vipi kwa ukamilifu na inafaa kutumika kigezo kipi katika uanishaji huu? Katika huu mjadala mrefu kuna makundi matatu ambayo aghalabu hujitokeza. Kwanza, kuna kundi la wataalamu linalopendekeza uainishaji wa nomino uzingatie misingi ya kimofolojia. Katika kundi hili kuna wataalamu kama vile Ashton (1944) na Welmers (1973). Wataalamu hawa wanadai kuwa nomino huainishwa katika makundi mbalimbali kwa misingi ya viambishi awali vya nomino hiyo, katika hali ya umoja na wingi, kama ilivyo katika maneno kitabu na vitabu, mtu na watu, mti na miti. Kundi la pili nalo hudai kuwa kigezo kikamilifu cha uainishaji huu wa nomino ni kile cha kisintaksia ambapo uainishaji wa nomino katika ngeli tofauti unazingatia upatanisho wa nomino husika na kiambishi cha kitenzi katika sentensi. Katika kundi hili kuna wataalam kama vile Adewole (1986), Kapinga (1983) na Mgullu (1999). Mtindo huu wa uainishaji ndio unaotumiwa katika mitaala nchini Kenya kwa sasa. Kundi la tatu nalo ni lile linalozingatia kigezo cha kisemantiki katika uainishaji wa nomino katika ngeli ambapo nomino hutiwa katika makundi ya ngeli tofauti kutegemea maana zao. Makundi ya kisemanti ni mengi na hujumuisha viumbe vyenye uhai k.v ng’ombe, samaki na makundi kama vile ya vifaa vya kazi k.v nyundo, ndoo, ngazi; sehemu za mwili k.v mgongo, mkono n.k. Hili kundi la uainishaji kisintakisia lina wataalam k.v Polome (1967) na Myachina (1981). Licha ya kundi hili kutumia semantiki kama kigezo cha uainishaji wa nomino hutumia nambari vile vile katika uainishaji wake (Mukuria 2002). Inaonekana kuwa kila kundi lina ubora na udhaifu wake. Kundi la kimofolojia kwa mfano, lina changamoto ambapo ni kweli kuwa kuna nomino k.v kitabu, mtu, mgongo zilizo na viambishi awali lakini kuna nomino zingine kama vile boksi na karai ambazo hazina viambishi awali na pia baadhi ya nomino husika huwa na upatanisho tofauti licha ya kuwa katika kundi moja. (Ashton 1944, Kapinga 1983). Kundi la kisintaksia nalo lina changamoto kadhaa, kwanza uainishaji wake ni wa kimofolojia vile vile kwa sababu unahusu vipande sauti vyenye maana yaani vipatanisho. Lakini tatizo kubwa zaidi ni kuwa sio vitenzi vyote vina viambishi vya upatanisho. Vitenzi vishirikishi kwa mfano, havina viambishi awali au tamati. Mwisho kundi la semantiki ndilo lenye changamoto kubwa zaidi. Ni vigumu kupata maana kamilifu kwa kila kundi linalopendekezwa na wataalamu hawa. Kwa mfano vifaa vya kazi huweza kuingia katika makundi mengi. Samaki huwa katika kundi la viumbe hai hata kama hayuko hai; jambo linalokwenda kinyume na mantiki ya kundi lake mathalan. Aidha ni vigumu kutoa maana kwa vikundi vya nomino kv ukuta,upote ama nomino zinazotokana na vitenzi kv kulima,kucheza,na kadhalika (Taz. Mgullu 1999; Habwe na Karanja 2004). Ufundishaji Kiswahili Kimatumizi Ili lugha ya Kiswahili iwe chombo kifaacho cha ustawi na maendeleo endelevu lazima ifundishwe kwa njia itakayozingatia matumizi halisi katika jamii. Ni bora matumizi yakaelekeza ufundishaji na kwa njia hii ufundishaji huweza kuakisi vipengele vya lugha na maendeleo yake. Imezingatia jinsi nomino husika zinavyofundishwa shuleni katika kiwango cha shule za upili kwa kuzingatia namna moja tu ya uanishaji na jinsi nomino hizi zinavyotumiwa katika baadhi ya maandishi na vyombo vya habari au hata matumizi ya kawaida ambapo huweza kuzingatia ngeli mbili au zaidi. Mbali na kitenzi, nomino ni kipengee kikuu cha lugha kinachotumika kiuamilifu kurejelea, kutaja, kuainisha, kulinganisha vipengele vya maisha licha ya kuleta upatanisho wa sentensi (Taz. Halliday na Hasan 1976; Beaugrande na Dressler 1981). Nomino za Kiswahili hata hivyo huweza kuainishwa kwa kuzingatia vipengele tofauti vya lugha kama tutakavyoeleza katika sehemu ifuatayo kwa mujibu wa watafiti mbalimbali. Lugha zote za Kibantu, Kiswahili kikiwemo huainisha nomino zake katika makundi ya ngeli. (Taz. Mgullu 1999, Habwe na Karanja 2004, Polome 1967, Myachina . Ngeli nazo humwelekeza mtumizi wa lugha namna ambavyo nomino hizo zitatumika katika upatanisho wa sentensi sahihi. Mtumizi akijua kuwa nomino kijana na mtu, kwa mfano, zimo katika ngeli moja basi upatanisho wake utakuwa sahihi. Idadi ya makundi haya ya ngeli hutofautiana kutoka lugha moja hadi nyingine. Kwa mujibu wa Greenberg (1966) nomino za lugha za kibantu kwa kawaida huwa na viambishi ngeli vinavyoonyesha umoja na vingine huakisi wingi, kv. ki - na vi – katika nomino kitabu na vitabu katika Kiswahili. Ingawaje ni kweli imebainika pia kuwa kuna baadhi ya nomino kv baba, mama, na hata shangazi ambazo hazina viambishi katika umoja na wingi na nyingine kv boksi, sanduku ambazo hazina viambishi ngeli katika umoja lakini zinavyo viambishi katika wingi. (Taz Kapinga 1983; Mbaabu 1992; Mdee 1986). Imebainika kwa mujibu wa wataalamu mbalimbali kuwa nomino huweza kuainishwa katika makundi mawili tofauti (Zawawi 1974; Mohamed 2002). Hata hivyo suala hili halijapewa uzito unaostahili katika ufundishaji wa ngeli katika shule za upili nchini Kenya. Katika shule nyingi nchini Kenya na katika hafla mbalimbali za wataalamu wa Kiswahili kwa mfano kuna malumbano ya kuainisha nomino kadhaa kv “maiti”, “mali”, na “maudhui”. Ni kama inaaminika kila nomino lazima iingie katika mojawapo ya ngeli ambapo itapata sifa zake za upatanisho wa ngeli husika hali inayoleta mgongano baina ya ufundishaji wa ngeli hizi shuleni na matumizi yake katika hali ya kawaida. Licha ya juhudi za awali kama vile Loogman (1974), Myachina (1981), Mgullu (1999), Ashton (1944), Mohammed (2001) na Zawawi (1974), utafiti wa kutosha haujafanywa, kubaini ni nomino zipi hasa zitaingia katika ngeli zaidi ya mbili na sababu za kuingia katika ngeli hizi ni zipi? Na je, nomino hizi zitafundishwa vipi shuleni ili wanafunzi wapate kuzielewa na kuzitumia ipasavyo? Je watumizi wa lugha katika eneo la Afrika Mashariki wanapaswa kuzitumia vipi nomino hizi katika mawasiliano yao ya kawaida bila kuwasababishia matatizo? Hali hii inapaswa kuonekana kama maendeleo au makosa ya lugha ya Kiswahili sanifu? Je ni kwa vipi uanishaji na ufundishaji usiotilia maanani matumizi huweza kukidhi mahitaji ya kimaendeleo? Ikiwa uanishaji kuwili utakubalika je, ni uainishaji upi utakaopendelewa katika maandishi yapi na kwa sababu gani? Haya ni baadhi ya maswali yanayoulizwa na kujibiwa katika makala hii. Ingawa walimu walidhihirisha uainishaji tofauti, hawakuzua suala la uainishaji kuwili wa nomino husika katika ufundishaji wao darasani. Hata nomino “maiti” ambayo aghalabu hujadiliwa sana katika vikao vingi vya walimu na wataalamu nchini Kenya iliainishwa kwa namna moja tu na walimu. Kila mwalimu akiianisha nomino hii kwa njia aonayo kuwa inafaa zaidi. Mjadala unaoendelezwa sana katika shule unahusu njia iliyo sawa na bora wala sio uwezekano wa kuainisha kuwili. Kuwepo na njia mbadala za kuaziainisha nomino hizi ina maana kuwa zinaweza kufundishwa na mwalimu akizingatia njia tofauti za kuziainisha. Lakini, je, kwa nini walimu hawakugusia suala la uainishaji kuwili hali matumizi yanaonyesha tofauti hizi? Huenda kuna sababu kadha wa kadha zinazopelekea kutofundishwa kwa uanishaji kuwili katika shule za upili za Kenya. Walimu katika sampuli ya utafiti huu huenda waliathiriwa na vitabu wanavyotumia katika kufundishia Kiswahili hususan suala la ngeli shuleni au hata makamusi wanayoyatumia kama vitabu vya rejea. Walimu hawakutoa nafasi yoyote ya uainishaji kuwili shuleni kwa nomino kv. karatasi, gari, zulia, taji, kamusi, nk. Swali kubwa likawa je, ni vipi wanafunzi watajua kuwa baadhi ya nomino za Kiswahili huainishwa kwa njia mbili tofauti? Na, je watakapotaka kutumia nomino hizi katika mawasiliano halisi watazitumia vipi bila kuchanganyikiwa? Ufundishaji wa uainishaji mmoja unakilemaza Kiswahili kama chombo cha maendeleo katika eneo zima la Afrika Mashariki. Zawawi (1974) anaunga mkono kauli ya nomino za Kiswahili kuainishwa katika makundi mawili tofauti au hata zaidi. Zawawi katika kuangazia suala hili alizingatia zaidi uainishaji nomino wa kimofolojia ambapo alisema neno shangazi kwa mfano, huweza kuainishwa katika ngeli tatu tofauti kama ifuatayo: Shangazi langu (Ji-ma class) Shangazi yangu (n-class) Shangazi wangu (m-wa class) Uainishaji huu umezingatia sana kazi ya Ashton (1944) ya kuzingatia viambishi awali vya nomino. Mohamed (2002) naye anapoangazia suala hili hili la uanishaji kuwili anazingatia sana, kama Zawawi (1974), mfumo wa ngeli kimofolojia kwa sababu anazingatia zaidi viambishi ngeli vya nomino za Kiswahili. Mohamed (2002) anahoji kuwa suala hili lina utata kwa sababu nomino fulani zilizo katika ngeli moja huwa na upatanisho tofauti kama ilivyo na nomino kijana, kiziwi, kiwete. Nomino kijana, kiziwi na kiwete kwa mujibu wa Mohammed (2002) zimo katika ngeli mbili tofauti ngeli ya (ki-vi) na (m-wa). Zimo katika ki-vi kwa kuzingatia mofolojia na m-wa kwa kuzingatia kwa kiasi kikubwa maana zake. Mtazamo wa kimofolojia hata hivyo hauzingatii upatanisho wa vitenzi na una matatizo mengi kama tulivyosema katika utangulizi. Lakini hata katika uainishaji wa kisintaksia kuna hali hii ya uainishaji kuwili kwa baadhi ya nomino za Kiswahili. Sababu moja kubwa ya uainishaji huu huenda ni analojia. Analojia husababisha miundo inayoingia katika lugha ya Kiswahili kutoka lugha za kigeni kuingizwa katika ngeli fulani. Uingizaji huu kwa kiasi kikubwa huzingatia umbo la nomino na wakati mwingine maana. Si ajabu basi neno hospitali limeingia katika ngeli ya( i – zi) maana umbo lake hufanana sana nomino za ngeli hiyo k.v habari, rangi. Vile vile nomino ambazo tayari zimeingia katika Kiswahili hujibadilisha na kuiga miundo na mitindo mingine kwa sababu ya kufanana kimaana na hata kimuundo. Kuna uwezekano mkubwa neno karatasi lilipoingia katika mfumo wa lugha ya Kiswahili limepewa ngeli ya (i-zi) kwa sababu ya kufanana na nomino za ngeli hii ambazo hazina viambishi ngeli k.v nyundo, ndoo, ngazi, n.k. Nomino karatasi, imeainishwa tena katika ngeli nyingine ambapo nomino za umoja hazina viambishi awali kv boksi na sanduku, n.k. Nomino karatasi kwa hiyo lina ngeli mbili tofauti kimatumizi kama ifuatavyo: a). i. Karatasi hii imechafuliwa (i-zi) umoja ii. Karatasi hizi zimechafuliwa (i-zi) wingi b) i. Karatasi hili limechafuliwa (li-ya) umoja Makaratasi haya yamechafuliwa (li-ya) wingi Matumizi (1a-1b) yanazingatia matumizi ya nomino karatasi kuwa katika ngeli mbili tofauti. Hizi ni ngeli za i-zi na li-ya. Hali hii ndiyo tuionayo katika matumizi ya nomino gari ambapo tunaweza kuwa na matumizi ya aina mbili lakini yasiyofundishwa shuleni kwa wanafunzi wa shule za upili nchini kenya. Tazama mfano ufuatao: a). i. Hili gari langu limezeeka sana (li-ya) umoja ii. Haya magari yetu yamezeeka sana (li-ya) wingi b) i. Hii gari yangu imezeeka sana (i-zi) umoja ii. Hizi gari zetu zimezeeka sana (i-zi) wingi Matumizi (2a-2b) yanaonyesha kuwa ngeli ya (i-zi) na (li-ya) hutumika sawia katika uainishaji wa nomino gari na husikika katika vyombo vya habari na maandishi ya vitabu vya Kiswahili na hata mitagusano ya kawaida. Kuna mfano mwingine zaidi wa nomino. Nomino makala husikika sana katika vyombo vya habari na watumizi mbalimbali wa Kiswahili katika eneo la Afrika Mashariki hulitumia kwa njia tofauti na kuonyesha kuwa kuna uwezekano kuwa limo katika ngeli zaidi ya moja. Hebu tuutazame mfano ufuatao: a) i. Makala hii imeandikwa vizuri sana (i-zi) umoja ii. Makala hizi zimeandikwa vizuri sana (i-zi) wingi b) i. Makala haya yameandikwa vizuri sana (ya-ya) umoja ii. Makala haya yameandikwa vizuri sana (ya-ya)wingi Mfano (3a-3b) unaonyesha kuwa nomino makala imo katika ngeli mbili (i-zi) na (ya-ya). Kwa mujibu wa dhana ya analojia, makala ni nomino inayofanana na nomino za (ya-ya) k.v magonjwa, maradhi, maudhui n.k katika umbo lake. Vile vile hufanana na maneno kama manowari ya ngeli ya (i-zi) katika umbo lake. Hivi watumizi huainisha nomino hii katika ngeli mbili tofauti. Hali hii ya kianalojia huathiri nomino zingine za Kiswahili lakini ambazo hazifundishwi kama zilivyo katika matumizi ya kawaida. Hali hii ya uanishaji maradufu ndiyo inayokumba nomino basi katika Kiswahili ambapo tunaweza kusema: a) i. Basi yangu imeharikiba (i-zi) umoja ii. Basi zetu zimeharibika (i-zi) wingi b) i. Basi langu limeharibika (ya-ya) umoja Mabasi yetu yameharibika (ya-ya) wingi Watumizi wengi wa Jumuiya ya Afrika Mashariki wanafahamu 4a na 4b ni matumizi mbadala na huakisi kitu kimoja katika mawasiliano. Je, ni njia ipi ya kujieleza iliyo sawa kuliko nyingine na sababu ni zipi? Ama njia zote ni sawa? Kama ni hivyo kwa nini walimu hawafundishi kuonyesha hali mbili tofauti? Nomino nyingine ambayo huelekea kuwa na uainishaji kuwili ni duka. Tazama mfano ufuatao: a) i. Hii duka inauza dawa (i-zi) umoja ii. Hizi duka zinauza madawa (i-zi) wingi b) i. Hili duka linauza dawa (li-ya) umoja Haya maduka yanauza madawa (li-ya) wingi Ifuatayo ni mifano mingine ya nomino za Kiswahili ambazo matumizi yake huashiria kuwa zimo katika makundi mawili tofauti ya ngeli. zulia (i-zi) (li-ya) dengu (i-zi) (li-ya) shati (i-zi) (li-ya) pua (i-zi) (li-ya) taji (i-zi) (li-ya) tumbo (i-zi) (li-ya) faili (i-zi) (li-ya) kamusi (i-zi) (li-ya) Matumizi haya hudhihirika katika vyombo vya habari,vitabu vya fasihi, makala mbalimbali na mitagusano mingine katika Jumuiya. Uainishaji huu huenda haufundishwi shuleni kwa sababu mbalimbali. Sababu ya kwanza huenda ni namna mitaala ya shule za upili inavyotayarishwa labda kupendelea uainishaji wa aina moja tu. Vitabu vya kiada ambavyo walimu hurejelea huelekea kupendelea aina moja ya uainishaji kuliko mwingine. Sababu ya pili ni kuwa huenda walimu huona kuwa uainishaji fulani ndio sahihi zaidi au sanifu zaidi kwa minajili ya ufundishaji wao. Kama ni kweli kuwa uanishaji mmoja ni sahihi zaidi hili ni suala linalohitaji utafiti mkubwa zaidi kubaini kati ya “faili hili” na “faili hii” ama “karatasi hii” na “karatasi hili,” kwa mfano ni tamko lipi lililo sanifu na bora zaidi? Kama ni hivyo kwa nini vyombo vya habari na watumizi wa kawaida pamoja na waandishi wa vitabu hutumia matamko yote mawili katika Afrika Mashariki? Mitagusano ya kimaendeleo inatambua matumizi tofautitofauti. Kwa njia hii lugha hukubaliwa kubadilika na hata kuendelea zaidi. Jukumu la kuwa kifaa cha maendeleo linatekelezeka kwa ubora zaidi kukiwa na mifumo mbadala. Kuna uwezekano mkubwa kuwa kuna walimu ambao hawajui hali hii ya uainishaji ipo. Wanajua uainishaji mmoja ambao labda ndio waliofundishwa wao wakiwa shuleni na ndio wanaofundisha shuleni wakiwa walimu. Kuna uwezekano pia wale walimu wajuao uainishaji huu upo huona itakuwa njia ya kuwakanganya wanafunzi hasa katika kiwango cha shule ya pili kuwapa zaidi ya uainishaji mmoja tu kwa hiyo njia ya kurahisisha ufundishaji ni kujikita kwenye aina moja ya uainishaji. Labda moja katika sababu za uainishaji tofauti ni athari kutoka katika lahaja mbalimbali za Kiswahili zinazotumiwa sambamba na Kiswahili sanifu. Ufundishaji wa nomino zinazoweza kuainishwa kwa namna mbili lakini zinazofundishwa kwa njia moja huweza kuvuruga uelewa wa Kiswahili na maendeleo yake. Hii itakuwa kwa sababu Kiswahili kitakuwa kinafundishwa shuleni tofauti na vile kinavyotumika katika hali halisi. Si ajabu basi uandishi wa miswada wakati mwingine huwa mgumu walimu wa shule wanapohusishwa ambapo huzingatia ngeli wanazofundisha shuleni tu. Katika hali hii walimu hawa huona ngeli ambazo hazifungamani na mafundisho ya shule si sawa hali inayoleta mtafaruko baina ya ufundishaji na matumizi. Watu wanaojifundisha lugha watakabiliwa na hali ngumu ya kuchanganyikiwa watakapokutana na watumizi wengine wanaoainisha na kutumia nomino fulani kwa njia tofauti na zao na kuona zao ni za makosa. Hali hii ya ufundishaji vile vile inainyima lugha ya Kiswahili utajiri wake wa kujieleza kwa njia tofauti. Kila lugha huwa na njia mbadala za kujieleza na hili ni suala ambalo lazima lizingatiwe. Lugha ya Kiingereza, kwa mfano ina, mabadiliko na hali ambazo zimetokana na analojia, neno brothers lipo badala ya brethren, neno dived lipo badala ya dove, neno chickens badala ya chicken yapo lakini hali hii hutokana na utaratibu wa lugha kutaka kuleta usare fulani katika na kurahisisha matumizi kwa kuiga mifumo ya kawaida katika lugha ya Kiingereza. Kila lugha lazima iwe na matumizi mbadala ila tu kwamba matumizi fulani yanaweza kutengewa eneo lake maalum lakini lazima yafundishwe ili wanafunzi wajue kwamba yako na jinsi yanavyopaswa kutumiwa katika lugha husika. Eneo zima la Afrika Mashariki litakuwa na mitindo tofauti ya nomino hizi na ni muhimu yote izingatiwe katika ufundishaji wa lugha darasani. Kwa hivyo ufundishaji unafaa kuzingatia hali mbalimbali, na mabadiliko yanayokumba lugha ikiwa lugha itatumiwa kama chombo cha mawasiliano mapana na chombo cha kuleta maendeleo katika eneo zima la Afrika Mashariki. Endapo ufundishaji wa lugha hauwezi kuonyesha hatua zote za lugha ni kwa vipi inaweza kudai kuwa ufundishaji huu unakidhi mahitaji yake? Hii ndiyo sababu tunapendekeza mabadiliko haya ili elimu iwe kwa kiasi kikubwa elezi badala ya kuwa elekezi ili iweze kutekeleza jukumu lake ipasavyo. Hitimisho Makala hii imechunguza changamoto za uainishaji wa nomino za Kiswahili katika ufundishaji wa lugha hii nchini Kenya. Imedai kuwa huku inabainika kuwa nomino fulani zinatumika kwa mitindo miwili tofauti katika hali ya kawaida, sivyo inavyofundishwa shuleni kwa wanafunzi wa Kiswahili nchini Kenya. Kwa hivyo wanafunzi hawapati kujua matumizi haya, jambo ambalo huvuruga uelewa wa ngeli na maendeleo na matumizi ya Kiswahili katika mawasiliano . Hali hii ya ufundishaji huenda inasababishwa na mitaala kupendelea mifumo fulani ya ngeli, na kuona kuwa njia inayotumiwa kuainisha nomino hizo ndiyo iliyo sawa kisarufi. Makala hii imependekeza kubadilishwa kwa hali hiyo ya ufundishaji ili lugha ifundishwe inavyotumika ili kuzizuke mgongano baina ya matumizi na ufundishaji wa ngeli za Kiswahili. Kwanza, mitaala ibainishe nadharia za sarufi na kuonyesha jinsi inavyojitokeza katika Kiswhaili. Pili, walimu watumie nadharia mbalimbali za sarufi kufundisha ngeli za lugha hii. Tatu, utafiti wa kina ufanywe kugundua matumizi ya Kiswahili katika mazingira tofauti. Nne, hali halisi ya Kiswahili itumiwe kuandaa na kufundisha mitaala ya Kiswahili. Marejeleo Ashton, E.O. (1944).
